Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Hajj: Obligation and Conditions of Istita'ah
Ruling with proof for Hajj obligation and its ten conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the ten Hanafi conditions for Hajj being obligatory (fard) and identify the Quranic and hadith proofs that establish each category.

Core Idea
Hajj is fard upon those with istita'ah—capability encompassing health, finances, safety, and family provision.

This passage from the Book of Hajj lays out the foundational ruling: Hajj is obligatory upon every free, adult, sane, healthy Muslim who has the physical and financial means to perform it. The author not only states the ruling but unpacks each condition with evidence from the Quran and Sunnah, showing that istita'ah is a multi‑faceted concept. Understanding these conditions is essential for determining when the obligation of Hajj actually applies to a person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the opening line: 'Hajj is wajib upon free Muslims, adults, sane, healthy, when they have the means.' Note that the commentary clarifies this 'wajib' means fard in the Hanafi school when conditions are met.
The matn uses 'wajib' but the sharh upgrades it to fard based on the Quranic dalil.
2
List the ten conditions for obligation
Identify each condition mentioned: freedom, Islam, adulthood, sanity, health, provision, transport, surplus beyond household needs, provision for dependents during travel, and a secure route. For women, add a mahram.
These are shurut al-wujub, not shurut al-sihhah.
3
Locate the primary proof (Quran)
Find the verse citation: 'Wa lillahi 'ala an-nas hijju al-bayti man istata'a ilayhi sabila' (3:97). Understand that this is the main dalil for the obligation itself, covering the general concept of istita'ah.
The Hanafis consider this a qat'i command (amr) in both thubut and dalala.
4
Trace the hadith proof for specific conditions
Examine the hadith from Ibn Abbas: a child, a Bedouin (pre‑migration), and a slave must repeat Hajj after becoming adult/migrant/free. This proves that Hajj is not obligatory upon children or slaves until they meet the conditions of adulthood and freedom.
The hadith also implicitly shows that health and travel ability are required, as the hadeeth addresses those who can physically travel.
5
Connect conditions to the concept of istita'ah
Observe that the ten conditions are a detailed unpacking of 'man istata'a' from the verse. Each condition—ability to bear expenses, physical capability, safety—is a necessary component of true capability.
This is a classic example of a mujmal (general) verse being made mubayyan (detailed) by the Sunnah.

Source Text

كان الفضل بن عباس رديف رسول الله فجائته امرأة من خثعم حاشیہ : (الف) اللہ کے لئے لوگوں پر بیت اللہ کا حج کرنا ہے جو اس کی طرف جانے کی طاقت رکھتا ہے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا جس بچے نے بھی حج کیا ہو پھر بالغ ہوا تو اس پر یہ ہے کہ دوسری مرتبہ حج کرے۔ اور جود یہاتی حج کر چکا ہو پھر ہجرت کی تو اس پر یہ ہے کہ دوسری مرتبہ حج کرے، اور جس غلام نے حج کیا ہو پھر آزاد کیا گیا تو اس پر دوسرائج ہے دیہاتی کو دوسری مرتبہ حج کرنے کا حکم اس وقت تھا جب ہجرت کے بغیر اسلام مقبول نہیں تھا، اب نہیں۔
Book of Hajj. [205] (1) Hajj is obligatory upon free Muslims, adults, sane, healthy, when they have the means. ... (Urdu commentary explains the meaning, evidence from Quran 3:97, and lists ten conditions for obligation: freedom, Islam, adulthood, sanity, health, provision, mount, surplus beyond household needs, provision for dependents during travel, and secure route. For women, also a mahram. Then a hadith from Bayhaqi is cited to show that a child or slave's Hajj does not fulfill the obligation; they must repeat it after becoming free/adult.)
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Hajj presents the ruling on the obligation of Hajj with its conditions and proofs. The type is a ruling with proof. The author first states the ruling: Hajj is wajib (obligatory) upon free, Muslim, adult, sane, healthy individuals who have the capability (istita'ah). The Urdu commentary explains the meaning of Hajj as a specific intention to visit the House of Allah. The primary proof is Quran 3:97: 'And [due] to Allah from the people is a pilgrimage to the House – for whoever is able to find a way to it.' This verse makes Hajj fard (obligatory). The commentary then explains that Hajj combines both financial and physical worship, and thus a substitute (badal) is allowed in necessity, but otherwise one must perform it personally. The author then lists ten conditions for Hajj to be fard: (1) freedom, (2) Islam, (3) adulthood, (4) sanity, (5) health, (6) ability to provide provisions, (7) ability to afford mount/transport, (8) having surplus beyond household needs, (9) provision for dependents until return, (10) security of route. An additional condition for women is the presence of a mahram. If all conditions are met, Hajj becomes obligatory; if not, it is not obligatory, but if one performs it anyway, it counts as fulfillment. The author provides proof for the conditions of adulthood and freedom via a hadith from Ibn Abbas reported in Sunan al-Bayhaqi: the Prophet said that a child who performs Hajj must perform another when adult, a Bedouin who performed Hajj before migration must perform another, and a slave who performed Hajj and then is freed must perform another. This shows that Hajj is not obligatory on children or slaves. For health, the commentary argues that a sick person cannot travel, so Hajj is not obligatory; but if one was healthy and became sick after Hajj became obligatory, he must make a will for a substitute. The hadith about the woman from Khath'am (mentioned partially) is a proof for the obligation upon those who can travel.

Key Terms
حج (hajj): The pilgrimage to the House of Allah (Kaaba) with specific rituals, combining both financial and physical worship.
استطاعة (istita'ah): Capability or means to perform Hajj, including provisions, transport, health, security, and fulfilling family needs.
محرم (mahram): A male relative whom a woman cannot marry, such as father, brother, son, uncle, etc., who accompanies her on Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi conditions listed in this passage, which of the following is NOT a condition for Hajj being obligatory?
A) Being free and Muslim
B) Being adult and sane
C) Being wealthy enough to afford luxury travel
D) Having a secure route and provision for dependents

Key Takeaway
Hajj becomes fard only when all ten (or eleven for women) conditions of istita'ah are satisfied, as derived from Quran 3:97 and confirmed by hadith.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Hajj Obligation and Its Conditions
Ruling on Hajj obligation with conditions and proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for Hajj being obligatory according to the Hanafi school and explain the evidence for each condition.

Core Idea
Hajj is obligatory only when one has provision, mount, surplus, safety, and health — ability is the key.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on when Hajj becomes obligatory. The source passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri enumerates ten conditions and provides proofs from Quran and Hadith. Understanding these conditions is essential to determining when the obligation actually applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State that Hajj is obligatory (wajib/fard) upon free Muslims who are adult, sane, healthy, and possess the means. Note that the ruling is conditional.
The author begins by listing the general categories: free, Muslim, adult, sane, healthy.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Cite Quran 3:97: 'And [due] to Allah from the people is a pilgrimage to the House – for whoever is able to find thereto a way.' The imperative indicates obligation; the condition 'istata'a' (ability) sets the threshold.
This verse is the foundational proof; all subsequent conditions derive from it.
3
List the conditions derived from hadith
The Prophet defined ability as provision and mount (hadith of man asking). The hadith of the old man shows health is needed. The hadith of Ibn Abbas clarifies that a child or slave's Hajj is not the obligatory one, reinforcing freedom and adulthood.
Each hadith addresses a specific condition.
4
Explain why surplus over basic needs is required
The commentary states that rights of people (family expenses, dwelling) take precedence over rights of Allah. Therefore, Hajj is only obligatory after fulfilling essential obligations to dependents.
This is based on the Hanafi principle that human rights (huquq al-ibad) are prioritised.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج [۲۰۵] (۱) الحج واجب على الاحرار المسلمين البالغين العقلاء الاصحاء اذا قدروا على الزاد والراحلة فاضلا عن المسكن ومالا بد منه وعن نفقة عياله الى حين عوده وكان الطريق آمنا
كتاب الحج کے سروری نوں حج کے معنی ارادہ کرنے کے ہیں۔ یہاں بیت اللہ کا ارادہ خاص انداز سے کرنے کا نام حج ہے۔ حج کا ثبوت اس آیت سے ہے ولله على الناس حج البيت من استطاع اليه سبيل (الف) ( آیت ۹۷ سوره آل عمران ۳) آیت سے ثابت ہوا کہ جس کو بیت اللہ تک جانے کی طاقت ہو اس پر حج فرض ہے۔ حج مالی اور بدنی دونوں عبادتوں کا مجموعہ ہے۔ اسی لئے مجبوری کے وقت حج بدل جائز ہے۔ بغیر مجبوری کے خود حج کرے۔ [۲۰۵] (۱) حج واجب ہے آزاد مسلمان، بالغ، عاقل ، تندرست پر جب کہ تو ے اور کجاوے پر قادر ہو۔ گھر کی ضروریات اور واپس لوٹنے تک اہل وعیال کے نفقہ سے زیادہ ہو اور راستہ مامون ہو۔ ش حج فرض ہونے کے لئے یہاں دس شرطیں بیان کی گئی ہیں (۱) آزاد ہونا (۲) مسلمان ہونا (۳) بالغ ہونا (۴) عاقل ہونا (۵) تندرست ہونا (1) توشے پر قدرت ہونا (۷) کجاوے اور سواری پر قدرت ہونا (۸) گھر کی ضروریات سے زیادہ ہونا (۹) واپس لوٹنے تک اہل وعیال جس کا نان و نفقہ حاجی کے ذمہ ہے اس سے زیادہ ہونا یا کم از کم اس کا انتظام ہونا (۱۰) راستہ کا امن والا ہونا۔ اور عورت کے لئے ایک شرط اور ہے۔ اس کے ساتھ ذی رحم محرم کا ہونا۔ یہ سب شرطیں پائی جائیں تو حج فرض ہو گا۔ اور یہ شرطیں حاجی کے پاس نہیں ہیں تو اس پر حج فرض نہیں ہوگا۔ البتہ جا کر کر لیا تو حج فرض کی ادائیگی ہو جائے گی۔ تمام شرطوں کے دلائل : آزاد، مسلمان، بالغ اور عاقل ہو تو عبادت فرض ہے ورنہ نہیں۔ ان کے دلائل پہلے گزر چکے ہیں (۲) سنن پھتی میں ہے عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله له ايما صبى حج ثم بلغ الحنث فعيله حجة اخرى، وايما اعرابي حج ثم هـاجـر فـعـليـه حجة اخرى، وايما عبد حج ثم اعتق فعليه حجة اخرى (ب ) (سن للبیھقی ، باب اثبات فرض الحج حج رابع ص ۵۳۳، نمبر ۸۶۱۳) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بچے اور غلام پر حج فرض نہیں ہے۔ تندرست ہو تو حج فرض ہوتا ہے ورنہ نہیں کیونکہ تندرست نہ ہو تو بیت اللہ تک کیسے جائے گا۔
(۱) آیت میں من استطاع فرمایا گیا ہے کہ جو بیت اللہ تک جا سکتا ہو۔ اور مریض آدمی بیت اللہ تک جا نہیں سکتا اس لئے اس پر فرض نہیں ہے۔ البتہ اگر پہلے تندرست تھا جس کی وجہ سے حج فرض ہوا بعد میں مریض ہوا تو اس پر حج بدل کرنے کی وصیت کرنا لازم ہے۔ صحت ہونے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عبد الله ابن عباس قال كان الفضل بن عباس رديف رسول الله فجائته امرأة من خثعم حاشیہ : (الف) اللہ کے لئے لوگوں پر بیت اللہ کا حج کرنا ہے جو اس کی طرف جانے کی طاقت رکھتا ہے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا جس بچے نے بھی حج کیا ہو پھر بالغ ہوا تو اس پر یہ ہے کہ دوسری مرتبہ حج کرے۔ اور جود یہاتی حج کر چکا ہو پھر ہجرت کی تو اس پر یہ ہے کہ دوسری مرتبہ حج کرے، اور جس غلام نے حج کیا ہو پھر آزاد کیا گیا تو اس پر دوسرائج ہے دیہاتی کو دوسری مرتبہ حج کرنے کا حکم اس وقت تھا جب ہجرت کے بغیر اسلام مقبول نہیں تھا، اب نہیں۔
على الزاد والراحلة فاضلا عن المسكن ومالا بد منه وعن نفقة عياله الى حين عوده وكان الطريق آمنا
... فقالت يا رسول الله ان فريضة الله عز وجل على عباده في الحج ادركت ابي شيخا كبيرا لا يستطيع ان يثبت على الراحلة افاحج عنه قال نعم وذلك في حجة الوداع (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب الرجل سمج عن غیر و ص ۲۵۹ نمبر ۱۸۰۹ر ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الحج عن الشيخ الكبير والميت ص ۱۸۵ نمبر ۹۲۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تندرست ہو تو حج کرے گا ورنہ اس پر حج فرض نہیں ہے۔ البتہ فرض ہو گیا ہو بعد میں بیمار ہوا ہو تو اس کی جانب سے ولی حج بدل کرے۔ تو شہ اور کجاوہ ہو تب حج فرض ہوتا ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عـمـر قـال جـاء رجـل الـى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال يا رسول الله ما يوجب الحج قال الزاد والراحلة (ب) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی ایجاب الحج بالزاد والراحلة ص ۶۸ نمبر ۱۳ ۸ر دار قطنی ، کتاب الحج حج ثانی ص۱۹۳ نمبر ۲۳۸۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سفر کا تو شہ ہو اور سواری پر سوار ہونے کا خرچ ہو تب حج فرض ہوتا ہے۔ مکان سے اور مکان کی ضروری اشیاء سے فاضل ہو اور واپس لوٹنے تک اہل وعیال کے نفقہ سے زیادہ ہو۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ سب انسان کی حاجت اصلیہ ہیں اور حج کے لئے حاجت اصلیہ سے فارغ ہو۔ کیونکہ یہ حقوق العباد ہیں اور حج حقوق اللہ ہے اور حقوق العباد حقوق اللہ سے مقدم ہوتے ہیں۔ اس لئے ان سب ضروریات سے فارغ ہو تب حج واجب ہوگا۔ اور راستہ مامون ہو تب حج فرض ہوتا ہے اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ راستہ مامون نہیں ہو گا تو حج کرنے کیسے جائے گا۔ من استطاع اليه سبیلا میں یہ داخل ہے کہ راستہ مکہ مکرمہ تک مامون ہوتا کہ بیت اللہ تک جاسکے (۲) جب تک مکہ مکرمہ تک جانے کا راستہ مامون نہ ہوا اس وقت تک حضور حج کرنے تشریف نہیں لے گئے ۔ حدیث میں ہے عن ابی اما مة عن النبي الا الله قال من لم يحبسه مرض او حاجة ظاهرة او سلطان جائر ولم يحج فليمت ان شاء يهوديا او نصرانیا (سنن بیھقی ، باب امکان الحج حج رابع ص ۵۴۶ نمبر ۸۶۶۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ظالم بادشاہ نہ روکے جس سے راستہ کے مامون ہونے پر استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے۔
الزاد : توشه راحلة : کجاوہ سواری۔ عود : لوٹنا، واپس ہونا۔
Book of Hajj. [205] (1) Hajj is obligatory upon free Muslims, adults, sane, healthy, when they are able to [provide] provision and mount, surplus to the dwelling and necessities and beyond the expenses of his dependents until his return, and the route is safe. ... Commentary: The meaning of Hajj is intention, specifically intending the House of Allah. Evidence from Quran: 'And [due] to Allah from the people is a pilgrimage to the House – for whoever is able to find thereto a way' [3:97]. It is a combined financial and physical worship. Conditions: free, Muslim, adult, sane, healthy, possession of provision, possession of mount, surplus to dwelling, surplus to family expenses, safe route. For women, additionally a mahram. If these are present, Hajj is obligatory; if not, not. Proofs: Hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'Any child who performs Hajj then reaches puberty must perform another Hajj, any Bedouin who performs Hajj then migrates must perform another, any slave who performs Hajj then is freed must perform another.' This shows child and slave not obliged. Health condition: hadith of woman of Khath'am asking about performing Hajj for her father, Prophet said yes. This shows health is condition. Provision condition: hadith of man asking what makes Hajj obligatory, Prophet said provision and mount. Surplus conditions: because these are rights of people, which take precedence over rights of Allah. Safe route: inferred from Quran 'able to find way' and hadith: 'Whoever is not prevented by illness, compelling need, or oppressive ruler and does not perform Hajj, let him die as a Jew or Christian.' Glossary: al-zad: provision; al-rahilah: mount; 'awd: return.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing the obligation of Hajj and its conditions. The author begins by stating the general ruling: Hajj is wajib upon free, adult, sane, healthy Muslims who possess provision (zad) and a mount (rahilah) beyond their basic needs and family expenses, and have a safe route. The Urdu commentary expands, noting that Hajj combines financial and physical worship, and can be deputised under necessity. Ten conditions are enumerated: freedom, Islam, adulthood, sanity, health, provision, mount, surplus over dwelling, surplus over dependents' expenses for the duration, and safe route. For women, an additional condition: a mahram (unmarriageable relative) or husband. The commentary then provides proofs for each: for freedom and adulthood, the hadith of Ibn Abbas stating that a slave or child who performs Hajj must repeat it after being freed or attaining puberty; for health, the hadith of the old man from Khath'am; for provision and mount, the hadith 'What makes Hajj obligatory? Provision and mount'; for surplus over necessities, the principle that rights of people (duyun al-'ibad) precede rights of Allah; for safe route, the Quranic condition 'istata'a' (ability) and the hadith threatening those who fail to perform Hajj without valid excuse. The commentary also addresses edge cases: if Hajj becomes obligatory then illness strikes, the person must make a will for a substitute. The tone is pedagogical, explaining each condition and its evidence.

Key Terms
الزاد (al-zād): Provision for the journey, including food and necessary supplies.
الراحلة (al-rāḥilah): Mount or means of transport, typically a camel or animal ridden.
محرم (maḥram): A male relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited (e.g., father, brother, son).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a condition for Hajj being obligatory?
A) Being male
B) Having surplus over dwelling and family expenses
C) Being under 50 years old
D) Having performed Umrah first

Key Takeaway
Hajj is obligatory only when one has the means: provision, mount, health, safe route, and surplus over dependents — ability is key.

Woman's Hajj Requirement of Mahram or Husband
Ruling on woman needing mahram or husband for Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman's obligation to have a mahram or husband for Hajj and apply it to given scenarios.

Core Idea
A woman's Hajj is obligatory only if she has a mahram or husband and the distance to Makkah is three days or more.

This lesson presents a foundational rule in Hanafi fiqh: a woman's obligation to perform Hajj is conditional upon having a mahram (unmarriageable male relative) or husband to accompany her, and the journey to Makkah must be three days or more. This ruling ensures women's safety during travel, rooted in prophetic guidance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The act is the obligation of Hajj for a woman. The condition is the presence of a mahram or husband.
Mahram: father, brother, son, etc. – someone she cannot marry.
2
Identify the distance threshold
The condition applies only if the journey from her starting point to Makkah is three days or more (approx. 48-100 miles classical).
If the distance is less, she may travel without mahram.
3
State the ruling
If condition and distance threshold are met, Hajj is wajib upon her. If not, it is not obligatory.
The ruling does not make Hajj invalid if she goes without, but it is sinful.
4
Consider the mahram's financial situation
If the mahram is available but refuses to spend, the woman must bear her own expenses. The obligation remains if she can afford it.
His refusal does not lift the condition of accompaniment, but he must not prevent her if she pays.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۶] (۲) ويعتبر في حق المرأة ان يكون لها محرم يحج بها او زوج ولا يجوز للمرأة ان تحج بدونهما اذا كان بينها وبين مكة مسيرة ثلاثة ايام او اكثر
اور عورت کے حق میں اعتبار کیا جائے گا کہ اس کے لئے محرم ہو جو اس کو حج کرائے ، یا شوہر ہو۔ اور نہیں جائز ہے عورت کے لئے که ان دونوں کے بغیر حج کرے جب کہ عورت کے درمیان اور مکہ مکرمہ کے درمیان تین دن کا سفر ہو یا زیادہ کا سفر ہو۔
عورت جس مقام سے حج کرنا چاہتی ہے وہاں سے مکہ مکرمہ تک تین دن یا اس سے زیادہ کا سفر ہو تو بغیر محرم کے حج فرض نہیں ہوگا۔ یا محرم ہو یا شوہر ہو جو اس کو حج کر اسکے تب حج فرض ہوگا۔ اگر کوئی محرم اپنے خرچ سے حج کے لئے تیار نہ ہو تو عورت کے پاس اتنا خرچ ہونا چاہئے
[206] (2) And it is considered for a woman that she have a mahram who performs Hajj with her, or a husband. And it is not permissible for a woman to perform Hajj without them if between her and Makkah is a journey of three days or more. ... And if the mahram is not willing to spend for Hajj, the woman must have enough expense.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: a woman's Hajj is valid and obligatory only if she has a mahram (unmarriageable relative) or husband to accompany her, and only if the distance to Makkah is three days' journey or more. The Urdu commentary clarifies that without a mahram or husband, Hajj is not obligatory, but if she has one, it becomes obligatory. If the mahram refuses to spend his own money, the woman must bear the expenses herself. This ruling is based on the principle of protecting women during travel, as found in hadith.

Key Terms
محرم (maḥram): Male relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited (father, brother, son, etc.) who can accompany the woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is a woman's Hajj not obligatory according to the Hanafi school?
A) If she is wealthy and has a mahram
B) If the journey to Makkah is less than three days
C) If she does not have a mahram or husband and the distance is three days or more
D) If she is above 60 years old

Key Takeaway
A woman's Hajj becomes obligatory only when she has a mahram or husband and the journey to Makkah is three days or more; otherwise, it is not fard upon her.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Conditions for Hajj Obligation: Provision, Safe Route, and Mahram
Listing conditions for hajj obligation with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions that make hajj obligatory in the Hanafi school and identify the proof for each condition from the hadith.

Core Idea
Hajj is obligatory only when you have surplus provision, a safe route, and for women, a mahram — these are the conditions of istita'ah.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri lays out the precise conditions under which Hajj becomes obligatory. It is not enough to have wealth; one must be free from primary needs, have safe passage, and for women, a mahram. The author provides hadith proofs for each condition, grounding the ruling in Prophetic guidance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hajj, which is fard 'ayn upon meeting conditions. State this clearly.
Hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime.
2
List the conditions for hajj obligation
From the text: (1) possession of provision and mount beyond basic needs, (2) safe route, (3) for women, a mahram or husband if journey is three days or more.
Basic needs include dwelling, indispensable items, and family maintenance until return.
3
For each condition, locate the dalil
The text cites: hadith of Ibn Umar (provision and mount), hadith of Abu Umama (safe route implied by absence of unjust ruler), hadith of Abu Sa'id (mahram for women). Identify each proof.
All proofs are ahad hadith and zanni in both transmission and meaning.
4
Understand the rational principle
The text explains that rights of servants (huquq al-ibad) take precedence over rights of Allah (huquq Allah). Therefore, one must be free from primary needs before hajj becomes obligatory.
This is a Hanafi legal maxim applied here.
5
Note the additional condition for women and its evidence
For women, hajj is not obligatory without a mahram or husband when the journey is three days or more. The proof is the explicit prohibition in hadith.
This condition is specific to Hanafi; Shafi'i allows traveling with trustworthy women.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على الزاد والراحلة فاضلا عن المسكن ومالا بد منه وعن نفقة عياله الى حين عوده وكان الطريق آمنا [ ۲۰۶] (۲) ويعتبر في حق المرأة ان يكون لها محرم يحج بها او زوج ولا يجوز لها ان يحج بغيرهما اذا كان بينها وبين مكة مسيرة ثلثة ايام فصاعدا [۲۰۷] ... فقالت يا رسول الله ان فريضة الله عز وجل على عباده في الحج ادركت ابي شيخا كبيرا لا يستطيع ان يثبت على الراحلة افاحج عنه قال نعم وذلك في حجة الوداع (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب الرجل سمج عن غیر و ص ۲۵۹ نمبر ۱۸۰۹ر ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الحج عن الشيخ الكبير والميت ص ۱۸۵ نمبر ۹۲۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تندرست ہو تو حج کرے گا ورنہ اس پر حج فرض نہیں ہے۔ البتہ فرض ہو گیا ہو بعد میں بیمار ہوا ہو تو اس کی جانب سے ولی حج بدل کرے۔ تو شہ اور کجاوہ ہو تب حج فرض ہوتا ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عـمـر قـال جـاء رجـل الـى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال يا رسول الله ما يوجب الحج قال الزاد والراحلة (ب) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی ایجاب الحج بالزاد والراحلة ص ۶۸ نمبر ۱۳ ۸ر دار قطنی ، کتاب الحج حج ثانی ص۱۹۳ نمبر ۲۳۸۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سفر کا تو شہ ہو اور سواری پر سوار ہونے کا خرچ ہو تب حج فرض ہوتا ہے۔ مکان سے اور مکان کی ضروری اشیاء سے فاضل ہو اور واپس لوٹنے تک اہل وعیال کے نفقہ سے زیادہ ہو۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ سب انسان کی حاجت اصلیہ ہیں اور حج کے لئے حاجت اصلیہ سے فارغ ہو۔ کیونکہ یہ حقوق العباد ہیں اور حج حقوق اللہ ہے اور حقوق العباد حقوق اللہ سے مقدم ہوتے ہیں۔ اس لئے ان سب ضروریات سے فارغ ہو تب حج واجب ہوگا۔ اور راستہ مامون ہو تب حج فرض ہوتا ہے اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ راستہ مامون نہیں ہو گا تو حج کرنے کیسے جائے گا۔ من استطاع اليه سبیلا میں یہ داخل ہے کہ راستہ مکہ مکرمہ تک مامون ہوتا کہ بیت اللہ تک جاسکے (۲) جب تک مکہ مکرمہ تک جانے کا راستہ مامون نہ ہوا اس وقت تک حضور حج کرنے تشریف نہیں لے گئے ۔ حدیث میں ہے عن ابی اما مة عن النبي الا الله قال من لم يحبسه مرض او حاجة ظاهرة او سلطان جائر ولم يحج فليمت ان شاء يهوديا او نصرانیا (سنن بیھقی ، باب امکان الحج حج رابع ص ۵۴۶ نمبر ۸۶۶۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ظالم بادشاہ نہ روکے جس سے راستہ کے مامون ہونے پر استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ الزاد : توشه راحلة : کجاوہ سواری۔ عود : لوٹنا، واپس ہونا۔ [۲۶] (۲) اور عورت کے حق میں اعتبار کیا جائے گا کہ اس کے لئے محرم ہو جو اس کو حج کرائے ، یا شوہر ہو۔ اور نہیں جائز ہے عورت کے لئے که ان دونوں کے بغیر حج کرے جب کہ عورت کے درمیان اور مکہ مکرمہ کے درمیان تین دن کا سفر ہو یا زیادہ کا سفر ہو۔ عورت جس مقام سے حج کرنا چاہتی ہے وہاں سے مکہ مکرمہ تک تین دن یا اس سے زیادہ کا سفر ہو تو بغیر محرم کے حج فرض نہیں ہوگا۔ یا محرم ہو یا شوہر ہو جو اس کو حج کر اسکے تب حج فرض ہوگا۔ اگر کوئی محرم اپنے خرچ سے حج کے لئے تیار نہ ہو تو عورت کے پاس اتنا خرچ ہونا چاہئے حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عبداللہ بن عباس فرماتے ہیں کہ فضل بن عباس حضور کے پیچھے بیٹے تھے کہ قبیلہ شم کی ایک عورت آئی ۔ کہنے لگی اے اللہ کے رسول حج کے بارے میں اللہ کا فرض بندوں پر نازل ہوا ہے، میرے باپ کو بوڑھاپا آ گیا ہے، کجاوے پر ٹھہر نہیں سکتا تو کیا میں ان کی جانب سے حج کروں؟ آپ نے فرمایا ہاں ! یہ معاملہ حجتہ الوداع کا تھا (ب) ایک آدمی حضور کے پاس آیا اور کہا یا رسول اللہ ا حج کس چیز سے واجب ہوتا ہے؟ آپ نے فرمایا تو شہ اور کجاوہ کے مالک ہونے سے۔
[The obligation is] upon provision and mount, surplus beyond the dwelling and what is indispensable, and beyond the maintenance of his family until his return, and the road be safe. (206)(2) And it is considered for a woman that she have a mahram to perform hajj with her, or a husband, and it is not permissible for her to perform hajj without them if between her and Mecca is a distance of three days or more. (207)... She said: O Messenger of Allah, the obligation of Allah upon His servants in hajj has reached my father, an old man who cannot remain steady on the mount; shall I perform hajj on his behalf? He said: Yes, and that was during the Farewell Pilgrimage. (Abu Dawud...) From this hadith it is known that if one is healthy, he will perform hajj, otherwise hajj is not obligatory upon him. However, if it had become obligatory and then he became ill, then a guardian may perform hajj on his behalf. Provision and mount: hajj becomes obligatory when one has them. Its proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar: A man came to the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, what makes hajj obligatory? He said: Provision and mount. (Tirmidhi...) From this hadith it is known that if one has travel provisions and the expense of riding, then hajj becomes obligatory. Surplus beyond the house and its necessary items, and beyond the maintenance of family until return. The reason is that these are primary needs of a person, and for hajj one must be free from primary needs, because these are rights of servants, and hajj is a right of Allah, and rights of servants take precedence over rights of Allah. Therefore, when free from all these necessities, then hajj becomes wajib. And the road be safe: then hajj becomes fard. Its proof is that if the road is not safe, how will he go for hajj. In 'man istata'a ilayhi sabilan' (whoever can afford the journey) is included that the road to Mecca must be safe so that he can reach the House of Allah. (2) As long as the road to Mecca was not safe, the Prophet did not go for hajj. In a hadith: From Abu Umama from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: Whoever is not prevented by illness, apparent need, or an unjust ruler, and does not perform hajj, let him die if he wishes as a Jew or a Christian. (Bayhaqi) This hadith argues that an unjust ruler preventing hajj indicates safety of the road. Provision: travel food; mount: riding animal; return: coming back. (26)(2) And for a woman, it is considered that she have a mahram who performs hajj with her, or a husband. And it is not permissible for her to perform hajj without these two when the distance between her and Mecca is three days or more. If the journey from her place to Mecca is three days or more, hajj is not obligatory without a mahram. Either a mahram or a husband must be with her for hajj to be obligatory. If a mahram is not willing to go for hajj at his own expense, then the woman must have enough expense to pay for the mahram... Footnote: (a) Abdullah ibn Abbas said: Fadl ibn Abbas was behind the Prophet when a woman from Khath'am came and said: O Messenger of Allah, Allah's obligation of hajj upon His servants has reached my father, an old man who cannot stay on the mount; shall I perform hajj on his behalf? He said: Yes. This was during the Farewell Pilgrimage. (b) A man came to the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, what makes hajj obligatory? He said: Possession of provision and mount.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri explains the conditions for hajj to become obligatory (wajib/fard). It is a ruling_with_proof passage. The author first states the conditions: provision (zad) and mount (rahila) surplus beyond basic needs like dwelling, indispensable items, and maintenance of family until return, and that the route is safe. For women, additionally a mahram or husband is required if the journey is three days or more. The author then provides proofs from hadith: the hadith of the old man (where the Prophet allowed hajj on his behalf, indicating that obligation is on the capable), the hadith of Ibn Umar defining obligation by provision and mount, and the hadith of Abu Umama linking hajj obligation to safety from unjust ruler. The Urdu commentary clarifies that these conditions are based on the principle that rights of servants (huquq al-ibad) take precedence over rights of Allah (huquq Allah). Thus, one must be free from primary needs before hajj becomes obligatory. For women, the hadith from Abu Sa'id and Darqutni emphasize the necessity of a mahram for travel of three days or more. The author refutes Imam Shafi'i's view that a trustworthy group of women suffices, arguing that hadith explicitly requires a mahram. However, if a woman performs hajj without a mahram, her hajj is valid but sinful, according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الزاد (az-zād): Provisions for the journey, including food and drink sufficient for travel to Mecca and back.
الراحلة (ar-rāḥilah): A mount or means of transportation for the journey, or its hire cost.
محرم (maḥram): A male relative permanently prohibited in marriage (e.g., father, brother, son, uncle) who accompanies a woman for hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling regarding a woman who has wealth but no mahram to accompany her for hajj when the distance is three days or more?
A) Hajj is not obligatory upon her until she finds a mahram.
B) She may go with a group of trustworthy women.
C) She must appoint an agent to perform hajj on her behalf.
D) She may go alone if the road is safe.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires surplus provision, a safe route, and for women a mahram for hajj to be obligatory, prioritizing huquq al-ibad.

Mawaqit: The Stations for Ihram
Lists the five mawaqit and ruling on passing them without ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five mawaqit and state the ruling for passing them without ihram.

Core Idea
Passing a miqat without ihram incurs a dam; the mawaqit are fixed by the Prophet.

When traveling to Mecca for hajj or umrah, the Shariah has designated specific points beyond which one must enter ihram. These points, called mawaqit, are established by the Prophet's hadith and are agreed upon by the schools. This lesson identifies the five mawaqit and the consequence of neglecting to assume ihram before crossing them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five mawaqit
From the hadith, learn each miqat and the region it serves: Dhul-Hulayfah for Madinah, Dhat 'Irq for Iraq, al-Juhfah for Syria, Qarn for Najd, and Yalamlam for Yemen.
Also note that these apply to anyone passing through those points, regardless of origin.
2
State the ruling on passing without ihram
It is not permissible (haram) to pass a miqat without ihram if one intends hajj or umrah. If one does so inadvertently, a dam (sacrificial sheep) becomes wajib.
The Hanafi school considers this dam as damm al-jabr (compensatory offering), not invalidating the hajj.
3
Recognize the proof
The hadith of Ibn Abbas is the primary dalil. The Prophet's specification ('waqqata') indicates obligation. The Hanafi view holds that this is a sunnah ahad with zanni thubut, making the ruling wajib (not fard).
Compare: the Shafi'i school also accepts these mawaqit but includes Dhat 'Irq as an addition by Umar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(207)(3) And the mawaqit which it is not permissible for a person to pass except in ihram: for the people of Madinah: Dhul-Hulayfah; for the people of Iraq: Dhat 'Irq; for the people of Syria: al-Juhfah; for the people of Najd: Qarn; and for the people of Yemen: Yalamlam. These places are at a considerable distance from Mecca. For the veneration of Mecca, it is necessary that when people from outside these mawaqit come to Mecca, they should enter ihram for hajj or 'umrah at these places. Then they perform hajj or 'umrah, then attend to their affairs. This is a requirement of the dignity of the House of Allah. And if one comes without ihram, then a dam (sacrificial offering) becomes obligatory upon him. Just as when one enters a mosque, the dignity of the mosque requires that he first pray two rak'ahs of tahiyyat al-masjid or some other prayer. (1) The specification of these places is in the hadith: From Ibn Abbas: The Prophet (peace be upon him) appointed for the people of Madinah: Dhul-Hulayfah; for the people of Syria: al-Juhfah; for the people of Najd: Qarn al-Manazil; for the people of Yemen: Yalamlam. These are for them and for anyone who comes upon them from elsewhere who intends (hajj or 'umrah). Footnote: (a) He said: A woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day is not permitted to travel for three days or more except with her father, brother, husband, son, or a mahram relative. (b) He used to say: A woman should not travel three days' journey or perform hajj except with her husband.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage concludes the section on conditions for hajj obligation and introduces the mawaqit (stations for ihram). It is a ruling_statement with proof from hadith. The author lists the five mawaqit for different regions: Dhul-Hulayfah for Madinah, Dhat 'Irq for Iraq, al-Juhfah for Syria, Qarn for Najd, and Yalamlam for Yemen. These are the points beyond which a person coming from outside must enter ihram before proceeding to Mecca. The Urdu commentary explains that this is for the veneration of the House of Allah, similar to offering tahiyyat al-masjid when entering a mosque. If someone passes the miqat without ihram, a dam (sacrificial offering) becomes wajib. The hadith of Ibn Abbas is cited as the primary proof for these locations. The footnote repeats the hadith about women traveling, but this is a later addition. The main focus is on the mawaqit and the ruling that passing them without ihram requires dam.

Key Terms
مواقيت (mawāqīt): Plural of miqat; specific places designated by the Prophet where one must enter ihram for hajj or 'umrah when coming from outside.
دم (dam): A sacrificial blood offering (usually a sheep) wajib as compensation for violating an ihram prohibition or omitting a wajib act like passing the miqat without ihram.
إحرام (iḥrām): The state of ritual consecration for hajj or 'umrah, marked by wearing special garments and abstaining from certain acts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must return to Dhul-Hulayfah and enter ihram.
B) He must sacrifice a dam (sheep).
C) His hajj is invalid – he must repeat it.
D) He must perform an additional 'umrah.

Key Takeaway
Crossing a miqat without ihram requires a dam (sacrificial offering) as compensation; the hajj or umrah remains valid.

Woman's Hajj Obligation Requires a Mahram
Ruling on woman's Hajj with mahram, including proof and Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman's Hajj without a mahram and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A woman's Hajj is obligatory only with a mahram; without one, she sins but the Hajj is valid.

This lesson examines a foundational issue in Hanafi fiqh: the role of a mahram in a woman's obligation to perform Hajj. The source text presents a hadith-based prohibition on women traveling beyond three days without a mahram, and then addresses the Shafi'i view that trustworthy female companions suffice. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi criteria for istita'ah (ability) and the consequences of violating the condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
What is the Hanafi position on a woman performing Hajj without a mahram? Determine the hukm level (fard, wajib, etc.) and the conditions for obligation.
The ruling is that Hajj is fard 'ayn but conditional upon having a mahram or husband.
2
Examine the primary hadith evidence
Read the hadith from Abu Sa'id (in Abu Dawud and Muslim). Identify the operative phrase ('la yahillu') and the exception clause that requires a mahram.
The hadith uses a general prohibition with an exception, which the Hanafi school interprets as a condition for permissibility.
3
Analyze the Hanafi istidlal (legal reasoning)
How does the Hanafi school derive the obligation from the hadith? The prohibition on travel without a mahram means that the ability to perform Hajj includes the availability of a mahram.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala, but used as a basis for the condition.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
What is Imam al-Shafi's argument? He allows travel with trustworthy women based on qiyas. How does the Hanafi school respond?
The Hanafi response emphasizes the explicit hadith and the risk of fitnah even with female companions.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
What is the difference in ruling? For the Hanafi, the woman who goes without a mahram sins but the Hajj is valid. For the Shafi'i, there is no sin if she has trustworthy women.
Both schools agree the Hajj is valid; the dispute is over sin and the condition of obligation.

It is permissible for her to perform Hajj with someone else if between her and Mecca there is a distance of three days or more. [207] (3) And the mawaqit that it is not permissible for a person to pass beyond without being in ihram: for the people of Madinah, Dhul-Hulayfah; and for the people of... he can take a mahram by spending on him for Hajj. Some scholars said: If there is no mahram, then Hajj is not obligatory at all. There is a hadith from Abu Sa'id who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'It is not lawful for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day to travel a distance of three days or more unless with her father, brother, husband, son, or a mahram relative.' (Abu Dawud, Muslim) And in al-Daraqutni from Abu Umamah: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'A woman should not travel a journey of three days or perform Hajj unless with her husband.' From this hadith it is known that a woman's Hajj becomes obligatory only when she has a mahram, because traveling without a mahram for more than three days is not permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i says: If she has trustworthy women with her, she can go for Hajj. We say: Traveling with women poses the risk of mischief, so it is prohibited, and the hadith also prohibits it. However, if a woman performed Hajj without a mahram, the obligatory Hajj is fulfilled, although she committed a prohibited act.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on a woman's obligation to perform Hajj. The author first mentions the condition of a mahram for travel beyond three days. The primary hadith evidence from Abu Sa'id and Abu Umamah prohibits a woman from traveling such a distance without a mahram. The Hanafi position is that Hajj becomes obligatory only when a mahram is available, as the ability to travel safely is a condition (shart) for obligation. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a group of trustworthy women suffices. The Hanafi response is that even with women, there is risk of harm (fitnah), and the general prohibition in the hadith takes precedence. The text concludes that if a woman performs Hajj without a mahram, her Hajj is valid and fulfills the obligation, but she has committed a sin (haram). This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi ruling: the act is makruh tahrimi, but the obligation is discharged.

Key Terms
محرم (mahram): A male relative whom the woman is permanently prohibited from marrying due to blood, marriage, or suckling.
حج بدل (hajj badal): A substitute Hajj performed on behalf of someone who is unable to perform it themselves due to death or incapacity.
استطاعة (istita'ah): Ability or capacity to perform Hajj, including financial means, physical health, and for women, having a mahram or husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of a woman's Hajj performed without a mahram?
A) The Hajj is invalid and must be repeated next year.
B) The Hajj is valid and she has not committed any sin.
C) The Hajj is valid but she has committed a sin.
D) The Hajj is not valid because she lacks a condition for obligation.

Key Takeaway
A woman's Hajj without a mahram is valid and fulfills the obligation, but she sins by violating the condition of ability (istita'ah).

The Five Miqat Stations: Their Ruling and Proof
Definition and rulings regarding the five miqat stations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five miqat stations and explain the Hanafi ruling regarding passing them without ihram.

Core Idea
Passing the miqat without ihram is a violation requiring dam, but early ihram is permitted.

This lesson establishes the five miqat stations as boundaries for entering ihram. Based on the Prophet's hadith, the Hanafi school rules that it is wajib to enter ihram before crossing these points. We will examine the proof and exceptions including early ihram and the rule for residents within the miqat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mawaqit
List the five miqat stations and the regions they serve: Dhul-Hulayfah (Madinah), Dhat 'Irq (Iraq), al-Juhfah (Syria), Qarn al-Manazil (Najd), Yalamlam (Yemen).
Dhat 'Irq was added by 'Umar for Iraq.
2
Understand the Hadith Proof
Read the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas where the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) appointed these places. Recognize that the verb 'waqqata' indicates an obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
The hadith is sahih and provides the textual basis.
3
Derive the Ruling
From the hadith, the Hanafi school derives that it is wajib to enter ihram before crossing the miqat. Passing without ihram is makruh tahrimi and requires a dam (penalty sacrifice).
The ruling is based on the command of the Prophet.
4
Note the Exceptions
1) It is permissible and even recommended to enter ihram before reaching the miqat. 2) Residents living within the miqat boundary (the hill) enter ihram from their homes, including the people of Mecca who start from Mecca for Hajj.
For Umrah, Meccans go to the hill (e.g., Tan'im).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And the mawaqit that it is not permissible for a person to pass beyond except in ihram: for the people of Madinah, Dhul-Hulayfah; for the people of Iraq, Dhat 'Irq; for the people of Syria, al-Juhfah; for the people of Najd, Qarn; and for the people of Yemen, Yalamlam. (1) The specification of these places is in the hadith from Ibn 'Abbas: The Messenger of Allah appointed Dhul-Hulayfah for the people of Madinah, al-Juhfah for the people of Syria, Qarn al-Manazil for the people of Najd, Yalamlam for the people of Yemen. These are for them and for anyone who comes upon them from elsewhere intending Hajj or Umrah. [208] (4) And if one enters ihram before these mawaqit, it is permissible. Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage covers the five miqat stations (mawaqit) established by the Prophet for those entering Mecca for Hajj or Umrah. The four main ones are: Dhul-Hulayfah (for Madinah), al-Juhfah (for Syria), Qarn al-Manazil (for Najd), and Yalamlam (for Yemen). For Iraq, 'Umar later fixed Dhat 'Irq. One must not pass these points without entering ihram. If one does, a dam (sacrifice) is owed. It is permissible to enter ihram before reaching the miqat, and doing so is considered better (afdal) as per a hadith from Abu Hurayrah. For those living within the miqat boundary (the hill area), the miqat is their place of residence, even for the people of Mecca whose miqat is Mecca itself (for Hajj, they start from their homes; for Umrah, they go to the hill). The text also includes a hadith margin note on woman's travel, but the main focus is the mawaqit.

Key Terms
ميقات (miqat): A specific boundary station where one must enter ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
حل (hill): The area outside the Haram but within the miqat boundaries; residents there enter ihram from their homes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person passes the miqat without entering ihram?
A) It is permissible if they have a valid excuse.
B) They must return to the miqat to enter ihram.
C) They must offer a dam (sacrifice) as compensation.
D) Their Hajj is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The five miqat stations are established by the Prophet; passing them without ihram requires a dam, but early ihram is permissible and residents within the miqat start from their homes.

The Five Miqat and Entering Ihram Before Them
Lists the five miqat and permits ihram before them

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five miqat and state the Hanafi ruling on entering ihram before them, including the evidence and preferred practice.

Core Idea
Entering ihram before the miqat is valid and even virtuous.

The miqat are the designated boundaries where pilgrims must enter ihram. The Prophet ﷺ established specific miqat for different regions. This passage lists four of them and adds a key ruling: if you enter ihram before reaching these points, your ihram is still valid. In fact, the earlier you enter, the better—the Prophet encouraged entering from home if you can bear the extra state of ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the miqat
Locate each miqat and its corresponding region: Dhat 'Irq (Iraq), al-Juhfah (Sham), Qarn (Najd), Yalamlam (Yemen). The fifth miqat (Dhu al-Hulayfah for Medina) is not mentioned here but is established elsewhere.
The hadith cited specifically confirms Dhat 'Irq for Iraq.
2
Understand the ruling on early ihram
The text says 'fa in qaddama al-ihrama 'ala hadhihi al-mawaqit jaza' – if he brings forward the ihram before these miqat, it is permissible (ja'iz). This means the ihram is valid and no penalty is required.
Ja'iz in Hanafi fiqh is equivalent to mubah (permissible).
3
Examine the dalil
The proof is the hadith from 'A'ishah: the Prophet designated Dhat 'Irq for the people of Iraq. Although the hadith only mentions one miqat, the other miqat are established by similar reports. The permissibility of early ihram is directly given in the matn.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for this ruling.
4
Note the preferred practice
While entering ihram before the miqat is valid, the sunnah is to enter at the miqat. However, the later Hanafi scholars (as per Urdu commentary) state that it is more virtuous (afdal) to start ihram from home if one can bear the extra state, as the Prophet ﷺ said completing hajj is to enter ihram from home.
This is an expansion (sharh) of the base text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العراق ذات عرق ولاهل الشام الجحفة ولاهل النجد قرن ولاهل اليمن يلملم فان قدم الاحرام على هذه المواقيت جاز عن عائشة ان رسول الله وقت لاهل العراق ذات عرق
Iraq: Dhat 'Irq; and for the people of Sham: al-Juhfah; and for the people of Najd: Qarn; and for the people of Yemen: Yalamlam. Then if he brings forward the ihram before these miqat, it is permissible. From 'A'ishah that the Messenger of Allah designated for the people of Iraq Dhat 'Irq.
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It first enumerates the five miqat established by the Prophet for different regions: Dhat 'Irq for Iraq, al-Juhfah for Sham, Qarn for Najd, and Yalamlam for Yemen. It then states that if one enters into ihram before reaching these miqat, the ihram is valid (jaza). The proof is the hadith of 'A'ishah which confirms the designation of Dhat 'Irq for the people of Iraq. The Urdu commentary clarifies that entering ihram before the miqat is not only permissible but better if one can bear the extra state of ihram, as the Prophet said completing hajj is to enter ihram from home.

Key Terms
ميقات (miqat): A designated boundary point where one must enter ihram for hajj or umrah.
جاز (jaza): Permissible and valid (the act is legally acceptable).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person from Najd enters ihram at his home before reaching Qarn al-Manazil, is his ihram valid?
A) No, it is invalid and he must go back to Qarn.
B) Yes, it is valid but he should give a dam.
C) Yes, it is valid and he may continue.
D) It is invalid unless he intended hajj from before.

Key Takeaway
Entering ihram before the miqat is valid (jaza) and, according to later Hanafi commentary, even more virtuous (afdal) if done from home.

Miqat for Residents Inside the Boundary and for Makkans
Ruling with proof on miqat for insiders and Makkans

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the miqat ruling for residents inside the miqat and for Makkans, and identify the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Those inside the miqat start from home; Makkans start from Makkah for Hajj and al-Hil for Umrah.

The miqat boundaries are fixed, but what if you live inside them? The Hanafi school, based on authentic hadith, provides clear guidance. Learn the distinction between the zones of hal and haram and where to begin your ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
First, identify the two categories of people discussed: (1) those whose homes are outside the miqat (they pass through the miqat), and (2) those whose homes are inside the miqat, including residents of Makkah.
The text focuses on those inside the miqat.
2
State the miqat for residents inside the miqat
The text says: 'Whoever is within them (the miqat), his miqat is from his family.' This means they can start ihram from their current location (the hal zone).
Hal is the area between the miqat and the Haram.
3
State the miqat for Makkans
For Makkans: For Hajj, the miqat is the Haram itself (they can start ihram in Makkah). For Umrah, the miqat is al-Hil (they must go outside the Haram boundary).
This is supported by the practice of Aisha (ra) going to Tan'eem.
4
Identify the proof
The text cites the hadith: 'Whoever is within them, his miqat is from his family, and likewise the people of Makkah enter ihram from there.' This is the dalil from Bukhari and Muslim.
The hadith establishes the generality of the rule.
5
Apply the ruling
Apply: A person living in Jeddah (inside the miqat) enters ihram from Jeddah. A Makkan performs Hajj from Makkah, but for Umrah goes to al-Hil (e.g., Tan'eem).
This distinguishes from those who must go to the miqat boundaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن كان منزله الحج والعمرة ومن كان دون ذلك فمن حيث انشاء حتى اهل مكة من مكة بعد المواقيت فميقاته الحل ومن كان بمكة فميقاته في الحج الحرم وفي العمرة الحل فمن كان دونهن فمهله من اهله و كذلك حتى اهل مكة يهلون منها
And whoever's home is (beyond) Hajj and Umrah, and whoever is within that, then (his miqat is) from where he begins, until the people of Makkah from Makkah. After the miqat, his miqat is al-Hil. And whoever is in Makkah, his miqat for Hajj is al-Haram, and for Umrah is al-Hil. So whoever is within them (the miqat), his miqat is from his family, and likewise until the people of Makkah, they enter ihram from there.
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the miqat for two categories: (1) those whose homes are outside the miqat (i.e., beyond the boundary) – their miqat is the miqat they pass; (2) those whose homes are inside the miqat (between the miqat and Haram) – their miqat is al-Hil, meaning the area where they are, so they start ihram from their current location. For residents of Makkah specifically, the miqat for Hajj is the Haram itself (they can start ihram from Makkah), but for Umrah their miqat is al-Hil (the area outside the Haram boundaries). The proof is the hadith from Bukhari and Muslim: 'Whoever is within them (the miqat), his miqat is from his family, and likewise the people of Makkah enter ihram from there.' The Urdu commentary adds that the practice of 'A'ishah going to Tan'eem for Umrah confirms the miqat for Umrah is al-Hil.

Key Terms
حل (hal): The area outside the Haram boundaries but before the miqat; the zone between the miqat and the Haram.
حرم (haram): The sacred territory of Makkah; it becomes the miqat for residents of Makkah performing Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person living in a city inside the miqat boundary wants to perform Hajj. Where should he enter ihram?
A) At the nearest miqat boundary.
B) From his home.
C) At the Haram boundary.
D) In Makkah.

Key Takeaway
The miqat for those inside the boundary is their current location (al-Hil); for Makkans, it is the Haram for Hajj and al-Hil for Umrah.

Passing the Miqat Without Ihram: Ruling and Proof
States the consequence of passing the miqat without ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on passing the miqat without ihram and identify the evidence from Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
Passing the miqat without ihram requires returning; if unable, a dam must be offered.

This lesson addresses a common Hajj scenario: crossing the miqat without entering ihram. The Hanafi school, based on the statement of Ibn Abbas, prescribes a clear remedy. You will learn the exact ruling and the proof that supports it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act of passing the miqat without ihram. What is the legal consequence?
The act itself is an omission of a wajib (ihram at the miqat).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The statement of Ibn Abbas (mawquf): 'Whoever forgets something of his rituals or leaves it, let him shed blood (offer a sacrifice).'
This is a Qawl Sahabi, considered a proof in Hanafi fiqh when not contradicted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this dalil prove the ruling? The general command 'falyuhriqa daman' includes the omission of ihram at the miqat, as it is a ritual of Hajj.
The imperative indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? The ruling is mukhtalaf fih; some schools may require a different penalty (e.g., hady) or consider the Hajj invalid. The Hanafi position is that dam suffices.
This passage does not elaborate on opposing views; the focus is on the Hanafi proof.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
What is the operative ruling for fatwa? If one passes the miqat without ihram, it is wajib to return if able; if unable, wajib to offer a dam.
This is the standard Hanafi position from the zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رأى ابن عباس يرد من جاوز المواقيت غير محرم عن عبد الله بن عباس انه قال من نسى من نسكه شيئا او تركه فليهرق دما
Ibn 'Abbas held the opinion that one who passes the miqat without being in ihram should be sent back. From 'Abdullah ibn 'Abbas that he said: Whoever forgets something of his rituals or leaves it, let him shed blood (i.e., offer a sacrifice).
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof addressing the consequence of passing the miqat without ihram. The statement of Ibn 'Abbas indicates that such a person should be returned to the miqat to assume ihram. If returning is not possible or the omission is via forgetfulness, the hadith from Ibn 'Abbas (mawquf) prescribes offering a dam (sacrifice) as compensation. The Urdu commentary elaborates that passing the miqat without ihram is not permissible and requires a penalty. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi position that missing a wajib (here, assuming ihram before crossing the miqat) necessitates dam.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A specific sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as a penalty for certain omissions in the Hajj rituals.
مواقيت (mawaqit): The designated boundary points for entering ihram for Hajj and Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person intentionally passes the miqat without ihram but cannot return to it?
A) He must still go back even if he is far.
B) He must offer a dam and his Hajj is valid.
C) His Hajj is invalid and must be repeated.
D) He must give sadaqah equivalent to the price of a sheep.

Key Takeaway
Passing the miqat without ihram is a wajib omission; if unable to return, a dam must be offered, based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas.

Miqat for Those in Makkah: Hajj and Umrah
Ruling on miqat for Makkans and crossing without ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the miqat for Hajj and Umrah for a person in Makkah, and explain the consequence of crossing a miqat without ihram.

Core Idea
Makkans begin Hajj in the Haram, but Umrah from the Hill; crossing any miqat without ihram requires dam.

This passage clarifies the miqat (appointed boundary for ihram) for those residing in Makkah. While non-Makkans have fixed miqats outside the Haram, a Makkan's miqat for Hajj is the Haram itself—he can tie ihram within Makkah. For Umrah, however, he must go outside the Haram to the Hill. The passage also warns that crossing any miqat without ihram obligates a dam (blood sacrifice) as compensation. The evidence comes from prophetic hadith and the well-known practice of Aisha at Tan'im.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
Two rulings: (1) The miqat for Hajj for a Makkan is the Haram; for Umrah, it is the Hill. (2) Crossing any miqat without ihram requires a dam.
The passage also addresses those who have settled in Makkah temporarily—they follow the same rule.
2
Locate the dalil
For Hajj, the hadith 'until the people of Makkah enter ihram from it' (Bukhari/Muslim). For Umrah, the hadith that Aisha was sent to Tan'im (a place in the Hill) to tie ihram.
The hadith for Hajj is a general statement; the Umrah proof is a specific incident.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'يَهِلُّونَ مِنْهَا' directly indicates that ihram begins from Makkah itself, not from an outside miqat. For Umrah, the Prophet's instruction to Aisha to go to the Hill establishes the rule for all Makkans.
This shows the Prophet differentiated between Hajj and Umrah miqats for Makkans.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may allow Umrah ihram from anywhere in the Haram. The Hanafi position is unique in requiring the Hill.
The dispute is based on different interpretations of the Aisha hadith.
5
Apply the ruling to crossing without ihram
If a person crosses any miqat without ihram, he must return to the miqat and tie ihram. If he fails to do so, he must offer a dam as penalty.
This applies to all miqats, not just those of Makkans.

Book of Hajj. After the miqats, so his miqat is the Hill. (6) And whoever is in Makkah, his miqat for Hajj is the Haram. This hadith indicates that whoever is inside the miqat, he should assume ihram for Hajj and Umrah from where he is proceeding, i.e., the Hill. At manzil: place of residence, home. Wajh. (210) (6) Whoever is in Makkah al-Mukarramah, his miqat for Hajj is the Haram, and for Umrah it is the Hill. For the people of Makkah and those who have settled in Makkah for some days, the miqat for Hajj is the Haram. Its proof has passed in the previous hadith: 'Whoever is inside them, his miqat is from his family, and likewise even the people of Makkah enter ihram from it.' (Bukhari, Bab Mahall Ahl al-Sham, p. 207 no. 1526, Muslim no. 1181). This hadith indicates that the people of Makkah will tie their ihram for Hajj from Makkah itself; they do not need to go to the Hill. But they will tie ihram for Umrah from the Hill. Because Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) came to Makkah and stayed, and thus became like a Makkan, but she was told to go to Tan'im for tying ihram for Umrah, which is in the Hill outside the Haram. And today Masjid Aisha is there. In a hadith: Jabir ibn Abdullah narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions... She said: 'O Messenger of Allah, you are going for Hajj and Umrah while I am going only for Hajj?' So he ordered Abdur Rahman ibn Abi Bakr to go out with her to Tan'im, and she performed Umrah after Hajj in Dhu al-Hijjah. (Bukhari, Bab Umrat al-Tan'im, Kitab al-Umrah, p. 240 no. 785? and Abu Dawud, Bab al-Muhabbalah bi al-Umrah Tuhayyad, p. 280 no. 1995). This indicates that Aisha went to Tan'im and tied ihram for Umrah, which is in the Hill. Therefore, for Umrah, one ties ihram from the Hill. If one crosses the miqat without ihram, then dam is obligatory. Ibn Abbas's opinion: 'He who passes the miqats without being in ihram is turned back.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi? Bab man marra bi al-Miqat..., p. 44). This effect indicates that one who crosses the miqat should be returned to it, because he should not proceed without ihram. In another effect: 'Abdullah ibn Abbas said: Whoever forgets or leaves out something of his rites should shed blood.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab man marra bi al-Miqat...). Footnote (a): And whoever is inside the miqat, he ties ihram from where he begins, even the people of Makkah tie ihram from Makkah. (b): Aisha said: O Messenger of Allah, you are going for Hajj and Umrah while I go only for Hajj? So he ordered Abdur Rahman ibn Abi Bakr to go with Aisha to Tan'im, and she performed Umrah after Hajj in Dhu al-Hijjah. (c): Ibn Abbas's opinion is that one who passes the miqat without ihram should be turned back. (d): Abdullah ibn Abbas said: Whoever forgets or leaves something of his rites should cause blood to flow, i.e., give a dam.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the miqat (appointed place for ihram) for those who are in Makkah. The author first states the general rule: for Hajj, the miqat of a Makkan is the Haram itself, while for Umrah it is the Hill (i.e., outside the Haram). The proof is drawn from two hadiths: one general that those within the miqat begin from their location, and a specific one stating that people of Makkah enter ihram from Makkah. The passage then elaborates that this applies even to those who have settled in Makkah temporarily. For Umrah, the example of Aisha is cited: she was instructed to go to Tan'im (a place in the Hill) to tie ihram for Umrah. This establishes that the miqat for Umrah for a Makkan is the Hill. The passage also addresses the ruling for one who passes a miqat without ihram: such a person must return and tie ihram from the miqat; if he does not, a dam (sacrifice) becomes obligatory. This is supported by the effect of Ibn Abbas, who says the person should be turned back and, if he neglects a rite, should offer a dam. The footnotes provide Arabic explanations for the hadiths and effects. Overall, the Hanafi position is clear: the miqat for Hajj for a Makkan is the Haram, for Umrah the Hill, and crossing the miqat without ihram necessitates a compensatory sacrifice.

Key Terms
ميقات (mīqāt): The appointed place (or time) for entering ihram for Hajj or Umrah; the boundary beyond which a pilgrim cannot pass without ihram.
حرم (ḥaram): The sacred precinct of Makkah where hunting and cutting trees are prohibited; the miqat for Hajj for Makkans.
حل (ḥill): The area outside the Haram, non-sacred territory; the miqat for Umrah for Makkans.
دم (dam): Blood sacrifice (usually a sheep) required as compensation for violating a miqat or omitting a wajib act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the miqat for Umrah for a person residing in Makkah?
A) The Haram itself
B) The Hill (outside the Haram)
C) The same as the miqat for Hajj
D) Any place within the boundaries of the Haram

Key Takeaway
For a Makkan, the miqat for Hajj is the Haram, for Umrah the Hill; crossing any miqat without ihram requires a dam.

Sunan Acts of Ihram and the Perfume Dispute
Listing the recommended acts before ihram and a Shafi'i dispute on perfume

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six recommended acts of ihram and explain the Hanafi position on applying perfume before ihram, including the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Applying perfume before ihram is sunnah even if its residue remains — the Prophet's practice confirms it.

This passage lists the six recommended acts (sunan) before entering ihram: ghusl, two garments, perfume, two rak'at, intention, and talbiyah. It also addresses a key dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i: is it permissible to apply perfume whose effect lasts into ihram? The Hanafi school holds that it is sunnah, based on the explicit practice of the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
List the six sunan acts
From the passage, identify each of the six acts recommended at the time of tying ihram. Note the evidence (hadith) for each.
These acts are sunnah muakkadah; omission does not invalidate ihram.
2
Understand the rationale for each
Why is ghusl preferred over wudu? Why two clean garments? Why perfume? The hadith provide the basis.
The Prophet performed ghusl, wore two garments, and applied perfume himself.
3
Identify the point of dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that perfume whose residue remains after entering ihram is impermissible. The Hanafi school disagrees.
The key is whether the residue leads to benefiting from perfume while in ihram.
4
Follow the Hanafi proof from hadith
Aisha's hadith shows the Prophet had visible perfume marks while in ihram. This is the core evidence.
The Hanafi response: the Prophet himself did this, so it is allowed.
5
Contrast the Shafi'i position and see the practical difference
Shafi'i requires that perfume be fully gone before ihram; Hanafi allows lingering scent. This affects pilgrim's preparation.
Thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi pilgrims can apply strong perfume before miqat; Shafi'i must use scent that fades quickly.

كتاب الحج
العمرة الحل [!] واذا اراد الاحرام اغتسل او توضأ والغسل افضل ولبس ثوبين جدیدن او غسيلين از ارا و رداء ومس طيبا ان كان له وصلى ركعتين وقال اللهم اني اريد الحج فيسره لى وتقبله منى ثم يلبي عقيب صلوته.

(۴) دو رکعت نماز پڑھے (۵) اور حج یا عمرہ کی نیت کرے (۶) نماز کے بعد تلبیہ پڑھے۔ حدیث میں ہے آپ نے احرام کے لئے غسل فرمايا عن ابن عباس قال اغتسل رســول الـلـه ثـم لبس ثيابه فلما اتى ذالحليفة صلى ركعتين ثم قعد على بعيره فلما استوى به على البيداء احرم بالحج (الف ) ( دار قطنی ، کتاب الحج ج ثانی ص ۱۹۷ نمبر ۲۴۰۸ سفن للبیھقی ، باب الغسل للا حلال ج خامس ص ۴۹ نمبر ۱۸۹۲۵ ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الاغتسال عند الاحرام ص ۷۱ انمبر ۸۳۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ احرام کے لئے غسل کرے یہ بہتر ہے۔ البتہ سہولت نہ ہونے پر وضو بھی کافی ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ احرام کے کپڑے پہنے (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن عبد الله بن عباس قال انطلق النبي له من المدينة بعد ما ترجل وادهن ولبس أزاره ورداء ه هو وأصحابه فلم ينه عن شيء من الاردية والازر (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب ما یلبس المحمر من الثياب والا ردیۃ والا زارص ۲۰۹ نمبر ۱۵۴۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کپڑے ازار اور چادر پہنے۔ کنگی کرے اور تیل یعنی خوشبو لگائے عن خوشبولگائے عائشة زوج النبي الا الله قالت كنت اطيب رسول الله لاحرامه حين يحرم ولحله قبل ان يطوف بالبيت (ج)(بخاری شریف ، باب الطيب عند الاحرام ص ۲۰۸ نمبر ۱۵۳۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ احرام سے پہلے خوشبو لگائے۔
امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ ایسی خوشبو نہ لگائے جس کا جرم احرام کے بعد رہے۔ کیونکہ اگر خوشبو کا جرم احرام کے بعد باقی رہا تو احرام کے بعد خوشبو سے فائدہ اٹھا نالازم آئے گا جو صحیح نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے ایسی خوشبو لگانا جائز نہیں جس کا جرم بعد میں باقی رہے۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ حدیث میں ہے عن عائشة قالت كاني انظر الى وبيض الطيب فى مفارق رسول الله لا الله و هو محرم (و) ( بخاری شریف، حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے غسل کیا پھر کپڑے پہنے۔ پس جب ذوالحلیفہ آئے تو دورکعت نماز پڑھی پھر اپنی اونٹنی پر سوار ہوئے۔ پس جب مقام بیداء پر چڑھے تو ج کا احرام باندھا (ب) آپ مدینہ سے چلے اس کے بعد کہ کنگی کی، تیل لگایا اور ازار پہنی اور چادر پہنی ، وہ اور اس کے ساتھی تو آپ نے ازار اور چادر سے نہیں روکا (ج) میں حضور کو احرام کے لئے خوشبو لگاتی جس وقت آپ احرام باندھتے اور اس سے حلال ہونے کے لئے بیت اللہ کا طواف کرنے سے پہلے (د) گویا کہ میں حضور کی مانگ میں خوشبو کی چمک دیک رہی ہوں اس حال میں کہ آپ محرم تھے۔
Al Sharh Ul Sameri, Vol. 1, p. 383, Book of Hajj. Umrah is the Hill. When he intends ihram, he should perform ghusl or wudu, and ghusl is better. He should wear two new or washed garments: an izar and a rida'. He should apply perfume if he has it, and pray two rak'at, and say: 'O Allah, I intend Hajj, so make it easy for me and accept it from me.' Then he should recite the talbiyah after his prayer. ... [reference text] This effect indicates that if he crosses the miqat and ties ihram without passing, he must give a dam. [1] (7) When he intends ihram, he should perform ghusl or wudu; ghusl is better. He should wear two new garments, or both washed, an izaar and a rida'. He should apply perfume if he has it. He should pray two rak'at. He should say 'Allahumma inni uridu al-hajj fayassirhu li wa taqabbalhu minni' (meaning). Then after the prayer, he should recite the talbiyah. There are six recommended acts at the time of tying ihram: (1) Perform wudu or ghusl; ghusl is better. (2) Wear two new garments. (3) Apply perfume. (4) Pray two rak'at. (5) Make intention for Hajj or Umrah. (6) Recite talbiyah after the prayer. In a hadith, he performed ghusl for ihram: Ibn Abbas said: The Messenger of Allah performed ghusl, then wore his garments. When he came to Dhu al-Hulayfah, he prayed two rak'at, then sat on his camel. When he ascended al-Bayda', he entered ihram for Hajj. (Darqutni, Kitab al-Hajj, vol. 2, p. 197 no. 2408; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Ghusl li al-Ihlal, vol. 5, p. 49 no. 18925; Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-ghusl 'inda al-ihram, p. 71 no. 830). This hadith shows that performing ghusl for ihram is better; however, if there is difficulty, wudu suffices. It also shows wearing ihram garments. (2) In a hadith: Abdullah ibn Abbas said: The Prophet set out from Madinah after combing his hair and applying oil, and he and his companions wore their izars and rida's; he did not forbid any izars or rida's. (Bukhari, Bab ma yalbasu al-muhrim min al-thiyab wa al-ridiyah wa al-izar, p. 209 no. 1545). This hadith shows that one should wear an izar and a rida', comb hair, and apply oil (i.e., perfume). (3) Aisha, the wife of the Prophet, said: I used to apply perfume to the Messenger of Allah for his ihram when he entered ihram, and for his halal before he circumambulated the House. (Bukhari, Bab al-tib 'inda al-ihram, p. 208 no. 1539). This hadith shows that perfume should be applied before ihram. Imam al-Shafi'i says: One should not apply perfume whose residue remains after ihram, because if the residue of perfume remains after ihram, then one would be benefiting from perfume after ihram, which is not valid. Therefore, applying such perfume whose residue remains afterward is not permissible. We say: There is a hadith from Aisha: 'I can almost see the white marks of perfume in the parting of the Messenger of Allah's hair while he was in ihram.' (Bukhari). So the Hanafi position is that it is permissible.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage lists the recommended acts (sunan) to be performed before entering the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah. The author enumerates six acts: (1) performing ghusl or wudu (ghusl being superior); (2) wearing two clean, new or washed garments – an izar (lower wrap) and a rida' (upper wrap); (3) applying perfume if available; (4) praying two rak'at of nafl; (5) making the intention for Hajj or Umrah, e.g., saying 'Allahumma inni uridu al-hajj...'; and (6) reciting the talbiyah immediately after the prayer. Each of these is supported by specific hadith. The hadith of Ibn Abbas shows the Prophet performed ghusl, prayed two rak'at at Dhu al-Hulayfah, and then entered ihram. Another hadith indicates the Prophet combed his hair and applied oil (perfume). The hadith of Aisha confirms she perfumed the Prophet before ihram, even when the perfume's effect remained during ihram. This leads to a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues that perfume whose residue remains after ihram is impermissible because one would be benefiting from it while in the state of ihram. The Hanafi response is that the Prophet himself had visible traces of perfume while in ihram, so it is permissible. Thus, the Hanafi school holds that applying perfume before ihram is a sunnah, even if its effect lasts into the ihram state.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): A ritual bath recommended before ihram; considered superior to wudu.
ازار و رداء (izār wa ridā’): The two garments of ihram: an izār (lower wrap) and a ridā’ (upper wrap); they should be clean and preferably new or washed.
تلبیة (talbiyah): The recitation of 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' after the intention and prayer, signaling entry into ihram.
طيب (ṭīb): Perfume applied to the body or garments before ihram; the Hanafi school permits its use even if residue remains.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the six sunan acts of ihram as listed in the passage?
A) Performing ghusl or wudu
B) Wearing two garments (izar and rida')
C) Reciting the Qur'an aloud
D) Applying perfume if available

Key Takeaway
The six sunan acts of ihram are confirmed by prophetic practice, and applying perfume before ihram is sunnah even if its effect remains.

Six Recommended Acts Before Iḥrām
Ruling on sunan of iḥrām with proofs and a dispute on perfume

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six sunan before iḥrām and explain the Hanafi position on applying perfume that leaves a trace, with proofs.

Core Idea
Applying perfume before iḥrām is sunnah; its lingering trace is no problem, based on the Prophet's practice.

Before entering the state of iḥrām, certain acts are recommended to prepare physically and spiritually. This passage outlines six such acts, supporting each with hadith. A key dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding perfume is also addressed, and the Hanafi response relies on explicit prophetic example.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six sunan
Scan the text to list the six acts: ghusl or wuḍū', wearing two clean garments (izār and ridā'), applying perfume, praying two rakʿahs, making intention for Hajj or ʿUmrah, and reciting talbiyah after the prayer.
Ghusl is preferred over wuḍū'.
2
Locate the dalīl for each act
Note which hadith supports each act. For ghusl and prayer, the hadith of Ibn ʿAbbās (the Prophet performed ghusl, prayed at Dhul-Hulayfah, then entered iḥrām). For garments and perfume, the hadith of Ibn ʿAbbās and ʿĀ'ishah.
The dalīl is from the sunnah (ahad hadith).
3
Analyze the perfume dispute
Imam al-Shāfiʿī argues that perfume whose trace remains after iḥrām is not allowed because one would benefit from it in iḥrām. The Hanafī respond with the explicit hadith of ʿĀ'ishah that she saw perfume traces in the Prophet's hair while he was muhrim.
This shows that residual perfume is not a violation.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilāf
The practical difference: Shāfiʿīs require perfume to be washed off before iḥrām if it would linger; Hanafīs allow it to remain. This affects the pilgrim's preparation.
5
Confirm the Hanafī tarjīḥ
The Hanafī position is muftā bihi because the explicit hadith overrides the general analogy (qiyās). The passage concludes that the hadith of ʿĀ'ishah is decisive.
Authority weight: ẓāhir al-riwāyah.
